id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_(South_West_England).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28South_West_England%29.svg/220px-United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28South_West_England%29.svg.png" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28South_West_England%29.svg/330px-United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28South_West_England%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28South_West_England%29.svg/440px-United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_%28South_West_England%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1277" data-file-height="1016" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_General_Election_2017_Results_Map_(South_West_England).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Election results in 2017</div></div></div>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 general election</a>, there was a 0.7% swing from Labour to Conservative in the region. For the region\'s electorate, 46% voted Conservative, 18% voted Labour, Liberal Democrats 15%, UKIP 14% and Green 6%. The Conservatives gained 15 seats almost all of which were from the Liberal Democrats.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2017" title="United Kingdom general election, 2017">2017</a> the Conservatives lost 3 seats (<a href="/wiki/Bristol_North_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bristol North West (UK Parliament constituency)">Bristol North West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Sutton_and_Devonport_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Plymouth Sutton and Devonport (UK Parliament constituency)">Plymouth Sutton and Devonport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stroud_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Stroud (UK Parliament constituency)">Stroud</a>) to Labour and 1 (<a href="/wiki/Bath_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bath (UK Parliament constituency)">Bath</a>) to the Liberal Democrats. Labour increased their share of the vote by 11.4% while Ukip\'s vote collapsed. However the Conservatives still dominate the South West with 47 seats out of 55.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2014_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 2014 (United Kingdom)">2014 European Election</a>, the <a href="/wiki/South_West_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South West England (European Parliament constituency)">South West England constituency</a> voted 32.29% for UKIP, 28.9% Conservative, 13.75% Labour, 11.1% Green, and 10.7% Liberal Democrat. UKIP and the Conservatives have two MEPs each, while Labour and the Greens have one each.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_England#South_West_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="List of schools in England">List of schools in England \xc2\xa7&#160;South West of England</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_education">Secondary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Secondary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The South West has a below average rate of attainment in GCSE (and equivalent) examinations, with the lowest regional performance in England from 2009 to 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-education.gov.uk_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-education.gov.uk-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, <a href="/wiki/South_Hams" title="South Hams">South Hams</a> had the highest percentage of pupils achieving 5 or more GCSEs at grade A*-C at 86%, whilst <a href="/wiki/Purbeck_District" title="Purbeck District">Purbeck</a> had the lowest at 70%.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The region has an above average rate of attainment in A-Level (and equivalent) examinations, having outperformed the <a href="/wiki/West_Midlands_(region)" title="West Midlands (region)">West Midlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands" title="East Midlands">East Midlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_East_England" title="North East England">North East</a> and <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-education.gov.uk_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-education.gov.uk-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_education">Further education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Further education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are around 29 <a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">further education</a> colleges in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Uni.of.bath.campus.arp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Uni.of.bath.campus.arp.jpg/220px-Uni.of.bath.campus.arp.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Uni.of.bath.campus.arp.jpg/330px-Uni.of.bath.campus.arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Uni.of.bath.campus.arp.jpg/440px-Uni.of.bath.campus.arp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1037" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Uni.of.bath.campus.arp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>University of Bath</div></div></div>\n<p>There are twelve universities in the region:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/The_Arts_University_Bournemouth" class="mw-redirect" title="The Arts University Bournemouth">The Arts University Bournemouth</a><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_University" title="Bournemouth University">Bournemouth University</a><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bath_Spa_University" title="Bath Spa University">Bath Spa University</a><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Bath" title="University of Bath">University of Bath</a><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Bristol" title="University of Bristol">University of Bristol</a><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Exeter" title="University of Exeter">University of Exeter</a><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Falmouth_University" title="Falmouth University">Falmouth University</a><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Gloucestershire" title="University of Gloucestershire">University of Gloucestershire</a><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/The_University_of_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="The University of Law">The University of Law</a><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Plymouth_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Plymouth University">Plymouth University</a><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Royal_Agricultural_University" title="Royal Agricultural University">Royal Agricultural University</a><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_St_Mark_%26_St_John" class="mw-redirect" title="University of St Mark &amp; St John">University of St Mark &amp; St John</a><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="University of the West of England">University of the West of England</a> (UWE)<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>There are also four higher education colleges. The region has the lowest number of people registered on higher education courses at FE colleges.\n</p><p>The University of Bristol receives the most total funding, according to <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Funding_Council_for_England" title="Higher Education Funding Council for England">Higher Education Funding Council for England</a> figures for the 2006/2007 academic year,  and the largest research grant\xe2\x80\x94twice as big as any other in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Bath has the next largest research grant, closely followed by Exeter. UWE and Plymouth get small research grants, but no other universities in the region receive much of a research grant. The University of Plymouth has the largest teaching grant.\n</p><p>Of the region\'s students (postgraduate and undergraduate), 50% are from the region, and around 40% from other regions. For full-time first degree students, 35% come from the region, around 22% are from <a href="/wiki/South_East_England" title="South East England">South East England</a>, and 8% are from London. Including the <a href="/wiki/East_of_England" title="East of England">East of England</a>, around 70% are from <a href="/wiki/Southern_England" title="Southern England">Southern England</a>. 10% are from the <a href="/wiki/English_Midlands" class="mw-redirect" title="English Midlands">Midlands</a>, and 5% from <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">Northern England</a>. The main access for students from the north is the <a href="/wiki/Cross_Country_Route" title="Cross Country Route">Cross Country Route</a>. Around 33% of native South West students stay in the region, with 18% going to the South East (around 60% stay in the south of England). Around 14% go to Wales, but very few go to the East of England. Access by road or rail to the East of England region is not straightforward, with around the same amount of travel as to Scotland. Many more native South West students are prepared to go to the north of England, than northern students are prepared to study in the South West. Once graduated, around 50% stay in the region, with 15% each going to London or the South East (around 80% find work in the south of England). Very few go elsewhere (especially the north of England); around 4% go to the West Midlands or Wales.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_media">Local media</span><span Parts of Dorset, including Bournemouth, Poole, Dorchester and Weymouth also receive <a href="/wiki/BBC_South" title="BBC South">BBC South</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meridian_Broadcasting" class="mw-redirect" title="Meridian Broadcasting">ITV Meridian</a> from <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">Southampton</a>. <a href="/wiki/Digital_switchover_dates_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Digital switchover dates in the United Kingdom">Digital switchover</a> from <a href="/wiki/Mendip_transmitting_station" title="Mendip transmitting station">Mendip</a> (for <i>Points West</i>) took place in April 2010, and for the <i>Spotlight</i> area it took place in mid-2009.</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Radio</dt></dl>\n<ul><li>BBC Radios <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Cornwall" title="BBC Radio Cornwall">Cornwall</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Devon" title="BBC Radio Devon">Devon</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Somerset" title="BBC Somerset">Somerset</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Solent" title="BBC Radio Solent">Solent</a> (Dorset), <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Bristol" title="BBC Radio Bristol">Bristol</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Wiltshire" title="BBC Wiltshire">Wiltshire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Gloucestershire" title="BBC Radio Gloucestershire">Gloucestershire</a>. National radio is from <a href="/wiki/North_Hessary_Tor" title="North Hessary Tor">North Hessary Tor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wenvoe_transmitting_station" title="Wenvoe transmitting station">Wenvoe</a> (west of Cardiff).</li>\n<li>Commercial radio stations are <a href="/wiki/Kiss_101" title="Kiss 101">Kiss 101</a> (Bristol), <a href="/wiki/Star_107.2" class="mw-redirect" title="Star 107.2">Star Solent">Heart Solent</a> (Bournemouth).</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Newspapers</dt></dl>\n<ul><li>Regional newspapers include the <a href="/wiki/Bath_Chronicle" title="Bath Chronicle">Bath Chronicle</a>, <a Journal">Salisbury Journal</a> (<a href="/wiki/Salisbury" title="Salisbury">Salisbury</a>).</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>During the 2016-17 season, the region had one <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> team (<a href="/wiki/A.F.C._Bournemouth" title="A.F.C. Bournemouth">A.F.C. Bournemouth</a>), and seven teams in the <a href="/wiki/English_Football_League" title="English Football League">English Football League</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bristol_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Bristol City">Bristol City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Rovers" class="mw-redirect" title="Bristol Rovers">Bristol Rovers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheltenham_Town_F.C." title="Cheltenham Town F.C.">Cheltenham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exeter_City_F.C." title="Exeter City F.C.">Exeter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Argyle" class="mw-redirect" title="Plymouth Argyle">Plymouth Argyle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swindon_Town_F.C." title="Swindon Town F.C.">Swindon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yeovil_Town_F.C." title="Yeovil Town F.C.">Yeovil</a>).  In the 2017/18 season they will be joined by <a href="/wiki/Forest_Green_Rovers" class="mw-redirect" title="Forest Green Rovers">Forest Green Rovers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The area\'s local football league is the <a href="/wiki/South_West_Peninsula_League" title="South West Peninsula League">South West Peninsula League</a> (SWPL). It was formed in 2007 from the merger of the <a href="/wiki/Devon_County_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Devon County Football League">Devon County League</a> and the <a href="/wiki/South_Western_League" class="mw-redirect" title="South Western League">South Western League</a>.  The league consists of a Premier Division of up to 20 clubs, which is ranked at Step 6 in the <a href="/wiki/National_League_System" title="National League System">National League System</a>, and two divisions at Step 7, Division One West and Division One East.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=South_West_England&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ons.gov.uk/ons/rel/regional-trends/region-and-country-profiles/region-and-country-profiles---key-statistics-and-profiles--october-2013/key-statistics-and-profiles---south-west--october-2013.html">"South West had the oldest population in the UK in 2012"</a>.
